SEC. 1601. TOWARD ZERO DEATHS. 
2
(a) IN GENERAL.—A local government, metropolitan 
3
planning organization, or regional transportation planning 
4
organization may develop and implement a vision zero 
5
plan to significantly reduce or eliminate transportation-re-
6

7

9

10
23, United States Code, may be used to carry out a vision 
11

13

14
(1) a description of projects or policies intended 
15
to significantly reduce or eliminate transportation- 
16
related fatalities and serious injuries within a speci-
17
fied timeframe, not to exceed 20 years, using exist-
18
ing transportation data and consideration of risk 
19
factors; 
20
(2) plans for implementation of, education of 
21
the public about, and enforcement of such projects 
22
or policies; 
23
00:22 Jun 12, 2020

364 
•HR 2 IH
(3) a description of how such projects or poli-
1
cies, and the enforcement of such projects or policies 
2
will—

(A) equitably invest in the safety needs of 
4
low-income and minority communities; 
5
(B) ensure that such communities are not 
6
disproportionately targeted by law enforcement; 
7
and 
8
(C) protect the rights of members of such 
9
communities with respect to title VI of the Civil 
10

and

(4) a description of a mechanism to evaluate 
13

15
demographic data. 
16
(d) INCLUSIONS.—A vision zero plan may include a 
17

18

(1) create a connected network of active trans-

SEC. 6006. STUDY OF FREIGHT TRANSPORTATION FEE. 
18
(a) STUDY.—Not later than 90 days after the date 
19
of enactment of this Act, the Secretary of Transportation, 
20
in consultation with the Secretary of the Treasury and the 
21
Commissioner of the Internal Revenue Service, shall es-
22
tablish a joint task force to study the establishment and 
23
administration of a fee on multimodal freight surface 
24
transportation services. 
25
00:22 Jun 12, 2020
H2
728 
•HR 2 IH
(b) CONTENTS.—The study required under sub-
1
section (a) shall include the following: 
2
(1) An estimation of the revenue that a fee of 
3
up to 1 percent on freight transportation services 
4
would raise. 
5
(2) An identification of the entities that would 
6
be subject to such a fee paid by the owners or sup-
7
pliers of cargo. 
8
(3) An analysis of the administrative capacity 
9
of Federal agencies and freight industry participants 
10
to collect such a fee and ensure compliance with fee 
11
requirements. 
12
(4) Policy options to prevent avoidance of such 
13
a fee, including diversion of freight services to for-
14
eign countries. 
15
(c) REPORT.—Not later than 1 year after the date 
16
of enactment of this Act, the Secretary of Transportation 
17

18

19

SEC. 8202. TRANSPORTATION OF LIQUEFIED NATURAL GAS 
10
BY RAIL TANK CAR. 
11
(a) EVALUATION.—Not later than 90 days after the 
12
date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator of the 
13
Federal Railroad Administration, in coordination with the 
14
Administrator of the Pipeline and Hazardous Materials 
15
Safety Administration, shall initiate an evaluation of the 
16
safety, security, and environmental risks of transporting 
17
liquefied natural gas by rail. 
18
(b) TESTING.—In conducting the evaluation under 
19
subsection (a), the Administrator of the Federal Railroad 
20
Administration shall— 
21
(1) perform physical testing of rail tank cars, 
22
including, at a minimum, the DOT–113 specifica-
23
tion, to evaluate the performance of such rail tank

SEC. 9509. FREIGHT TRAIN CREW SIZE SAFETY STANDARDS. 
3
(a) IN GENERAL.—Subchapter II of chapter 201 of 
4
title 49, United States Code, is amended by adding at the 
5
end the following: 
6
‘‘§ 20169. Freight train crew size safety standards 
7
‘‘(a) MINIMUM CREW SIZE.—No freight train may be 
8
operated unless such train has a crew of at least 1 appro-
9
priately qualified and certified conductor and 1 appro-
10
priately qualified and certified engineer. 
11
‘‘(b) EXCEPTIONS.—Except as provided in subsection 
12
(d), the prohibition in subsection (a) shall not apply in 
13
the following circumstances: 
14
‘‘(1) Train operations within a rail yard or ter-
15
minal area or on auxiliary or industry tracks. 
16
‘‘(2) A train operated— 
17
‘‘(A) by a railroad carrier that has fewer 
18
than 400,000 total employee work hours annu-
19
ally and less than $20,000,000 annual revenue; 
20
‘‘(B) at a speed of not more than 25 miles 
21
per hour; and 
22
‘‘(C) on a track with an average track 
23
grade of less than 2 percent for any segment of 
24
track that is at least 2 continuous miles. 
25
00:22 Jun 12, 2020
H2
836 
•HR 2 IH
‘‘(3) Locomotives performing assistance to a 
1
train that has incurred mechanical failure or lacks 
2
the power to traverse difficult terrain, including 
3
traveling to or from the location where assistance is 
4
provided. 
5
‘‘(4) Locomotives that— 
6
‘‘(A) are not attached to any equipment or 
7
attached only to a caboose; and 
8
‘‘(B) do not travel farther than 30 miles 
9
from a rail yard. 
10
‘‘(5) Train operations staffed with fewer than a 
11
2-person crew at least 1 year prior to the date of en-
12
actment of this section, if the Secretary determines 
13
that the operation achieves an equivalent level of 
14
safety. 
15
‘‘(c) TRAINS INELIGIBLE FOR EXCEPTION.—The ex-
16
ceptions under subsection (b) may not be applied to— 
17
‘‘(1) a train transporting 1 or more loaded cars 
18
carrying material toxic by inhalation, as defined in 
19
section 171.8 of title 49, Code of Federal Regula-
20
tions; 
21
‘‘(2) a train carrying 20 or more loaded tank 
22
cars of a Class 2 material or a Class 3 flammable 
23
liquid in a continuous block or a single train car-
24
rying 35 or more loaded tank cars of a Class 2 ma-
25
00:22 Jun 12, 2020
H2
837 
•HR 2 IH
terial or a Class 3 flammable liquid throughout the 
1
train consist; and 
2
‘‘(3) a train with a total length of 7,500 feet or

5

6
20103(d).’’.

SEC. 9553. ESTABLISHMENT OF 10-MINUTE TIME LIMIT FOR 
1
BLOCKING PUBLIC GRADE CROSSINGS. 
2
(a) IN GENERAL.—Subchapter II of chapter 201 of 
3
title 49, United States Code, as amended by this division, 
4
is further amended by adding at the end the following: 
5
‘‘§ 20173. Time limit for blocking a rail crossing 
6
‘‘(a) TIME LIMIT.—A train, locomotive, railroad car, 
7
or other rail equipment is prohibited from blocking a 
8
crossing for more than 10 minutes, unless the train, loco-
9
motive, or other equipment is directly delayed by— 
10
‘‘(1) a casualty or serious injury; 
11
‘‘(2) an accident; 
12
‘‘(3) a track obstruction; 
13
‘‘(4) an act of God; or 
14
‘‘(5) a derailment or a major equipment failure 
15
that prevents the train from advancing. 
16
‘‘(b) CIVIL PENALTY.—The Secretary of Transpor-
17
tation may issue civil penalties for violations of subsection 
18
(a) in accordance with section 21301. 
19
‘‘(c) DELEGATION.—The Secretary may delegate en-
20
forcement actions under subsection (b) to States either 
21
through a State inspector certified by the Federal Rail-
22
road Administration, or other law enforcement officials as 
23
designated by the States and approved by the Administra-
24
tion. The Secretary shall issue guidance or regulations not 
25
later than 1 year after the date of enactment on the cri-
26
00:22 Jun 12, 2020
H2
860 
•HR 2 IH
teria and process for States to gain approval under this 
1
section. 
2
‘‘(d) APPLICATION
TO AMTRAK
AND COMMUTER 
3
RAILROADS.—This section shall not apply to Amtrak or 
4
commuter authorities, including Amtrak and commuter 
5
authorities’ operations run or dispatched by a Class I rail-
6
road. 
7
‘‘(e) DEFINITIONS.—In this section: 
8
‘‘(1) CROSSING.—The term ‘crossing’ means a 
9
location within a State in which a public highway, 
10
road, or street, including associated sidewalks and 
11
pathways, crosses 1 or more railroad tracks either at 
12
grade or grade-separated. 
13
‘‘(2) BLOCKED CROSSING.—The term ‘blocked 
14
crossing’ means a circumstance in which a train, lo-
15
comotive, railroad car, or other rail equipment is 
16

17
